        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Steps from the video:



<span class="line"><!---->Steps from the video:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Open Chrome with --no-sandbox



<span class="line"><!---->1. Open Chrome with --no-sandbox<!----></span>



<br>





2. Go to chrome://tracing



<span class="line"><!---->2. Go to chrome://tracing<!----></span>



<br>





3. Click Record



<span class="line"><!---->3. Click Record<!----></span>



<br>





4. Click Edit Categories



<span class="line"><!---->4. Click Edit Categories<!----></span>



<br>





5. Click "All" above the 'disabled by default categories'



<span class="line"><!---->5. Click "All" above the 'disabled by default categories'<!----></span>



<br>





6. Click Record



<span class="line"><!---->6. Click Record<!----></span>



<br>





7. Immediately click Load



<span class="line"><!---->7. Immediately click Load<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I can't reproduce this on asan-linux-release-970999. I'll have a try on Windows in case it's platform-specific or that alters the timing.



<span class="line"><!---->I can't reproduce this on asan-linux-release-970999. I'll have a try on Windows in case it's platform-specific or that alters the timing.<!----></span>

1) please could you comment on whether this tracing can be enabled via any other means than via the series of UI clicks above. It is not plausible for a remote website to entice users to go through that series of clicks, and so this would be a non-security bug. However if this tracing can be enabled via extension APIs or via any other means then maybe it's valid. I will err on the side of caution and label this as a security bug, but we should flip to type=Bug if this is the only way to reach this OOB.

I don't think it's a security issue because it can't be triggered via executing JS code. The crash happens in the code that collects statistics about allocated objects.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think it's a security issue because it can't be triggered via executing JS code. The crash happens in the code that collects statistics about allocated objects.<!----></span>

However, the fix must be merged to M100 in order to avoid crashes when collecting V8 heap stats.



<span class="line"><!---->However, the fix must be merged to M100 in order to avoid crashes when collecting V8 heap stats.<!----></span>

          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */

          display: block;
